  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5ae65527-f3c7-4483-aee8-59e1c1f451a7'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer5501281891322511329">Sixteen-year-old Neryn is alone in the land of Alban, where the oppressive king has ordered anyone with magical strengths captured and brought before him. Eager to hide her own canny skill--a uniquely powerful ability to communicate with the fairy-like Good Folk--Neryn sets out for the legendary Shadowfell, a home and training ground for a secret rebel group determined to </span>
  <span id="freeText5501281891322511329" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Neryn is alone in the land of Alban, where the oppressive king has ordered anyone with magical strengths captured and brought before him. Eager to hide her own canny skill--a uniquely powerful ability to communicate with the fairy-like Good Folk--Neryn sets out for the legendary Shadowfell, a home and training ground for a secret rebel group determined to overthrow the evil King Keldec. <br /><br />During her dangerous journey, she receives aid from the Good Folk, who tell her she must pass a series of tests in order to recognize her full potential. She also finds help from a handsome young man, Flint, who rescues her from certain death--but whose motives in doing so remain unclear. Neryn struggles to trust her only allies. They both hint that she alone may be the key to Alban's release from Keldec's rule. Homeless, unsure of who to trust, and trapped in an empire determined to crush her, Neryn must make it to Shadowfell not only to save herself, but to save Alban.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Though this is a fantasy novel, "Alban" or, as it is sometimes called, "Alba" is the ancient name for Scotland (just as Eire or Erin are the Ancient n<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Though this is a fantasy novel, "Alban" or, as it is sometimes called, "Alba" is the ancient name for Scotland (just as Eire or Erin are the Ancient names for Ireland), so I would hazard a guess that this is set in an "alternate" Scotland that resembles something akin to pre-medieval to early medieval times, well before the Nordic, Roman and Norman invasions of the Brittish Isles.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">A specific age is not given. Neryn guesses that he is 5-6 years older than her, and then his age is hinted at again in relation to where he was when t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">A specific age is not given. Neryn guesses that he is 5-6 years older than her, and then his age is hinted at again in relation to where he was when the king began his reign. So about 20-21.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_277845849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277845849" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277845849?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=the-great-shelf-of-meh">the-great-shelf-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=australian-writer">australian-writer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277845849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4983215868608569105">There is some­thing inef­fa­bly mag­i­cal about Marillier’s nov­els. There are pre­cious few authors, in my opin­ion, who cre­ate as earnest a fan­tasy envi­ron­ment replete with mys­ti­cism and magic as Mar­il­lier does.<br/><br/>I feel a lit­tle embar­rassed and ashamed. I was des­per­ate for this book. After lov­ing Wild­wood Danc­ing and Heart’s Blood with a fiery pas­sion, I was sure I’d adore this one too.<br/><br/>The first thing that you should know about Shad­owfell is that it’s not as much the same ilk as</span>
  <span id="freeText4983215868608569105" style="display:none">There is some­thing inef­fa­bly mag­i­cal about Marillier’s nov­els. There are pre­cious few authors, in my opin­ion, who cre­ate as earnest a fan­tasy envi­ron­ment replete with mys­ti­cism and magic as Mar­il­lier does.<br /><br />I feel a lit­tle embar­rassed and ashamed. I was des­per­ate for this book. After lov­ing Wild­wood Danc­ing and Heart’s Blood with a fiery pas­sion, I was sure I’d adore this one too.<br /><br />The first thing that you should know about Shad­owfell is that it’s not as much the same ilk as Wild­wood Danc­ing and Heart’s Blood. It’s closer to her Daugh­ter of the For­est series in tone and story telling though less adult. The sec­ond thing you should know is that the pace and story telling of this novel is even slower than that of Daugh­ter of the For­est. If you’re not famil­iar with Marillier’s prior work then you will need to con­sider where the aspects of Lord of the Rings series in which Sam and Frodo were walk­ing to Mor­dor were some­thing you enjoyed as a reader. If they weren’t then I would highly advise you give this a skip. In fact, if you’re not a fan of walk­ing in gen­eral then give this book a skip – there was a lot of damn walk­ing in this book. A LOT.<br /><br />Whilst the prose and char­ac­ters and sus­pense made up for a lot of the stag­na­tion in plot – it didn’t always feel enough to carry the novel enough for me to give it four stars. Neryn’s char­ac­ter in par­tic­u­lar gave me great pause. Marillier’s female pro­tag­o­nists are often strong, capa­ble, wise and dig­ni­fied. That’s just the way she writes them and I love her for that. But Neryn lacked the spark of per­son­al­ity, of sub­stance that I usu­ally enjoy. She has no real flaws – unless you count not being able to trust a man who she has no rea­son to trust (I call that com­mon sense). Per­haps she has a whole breadth of char­ac­ter that we haven’t seen yet. I don’t know. This novel doesn’t afford her to show much since she lives in a con­stant state of sur­vival mode.<br /><br />Over all, I would still pick this novel up over a whole host of nov­els, but for a Mar­il­lier novel, I felt a tad let down. I’m hop­ing the next in the series shall rec­tify that and con­tain a great deal less walking.<br /><br /><i>*This book was provided to me by the publisher.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4983215868608569105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1059862883" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059862883" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059862883?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059862883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3930366561053354029"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611355._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>3.5 stars.</u>
</b> If I had to choose a word to describe it I'd say that this book is ... <b>quiet</b>. Look, quiet is not necessarily a bad thing - it brings a different atmosphere along its path, almost soothing and <b>completely enchanting</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611357._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>① <b>There is a lot of walking in this book</b>, and when I say <i>a lot</i>, picture Frodo and Sam wandering in the Middle-Earth. <i>That</i> kind of walking. <br/><br/>② <b>The plot is incredibly repetitive</b>, the whole book revolving around the fact that a) Neryn has to go to Shadowfell, b) she doesn't </span>
  <span id="freeText3930366561053354029" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611355._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>3.5 stars.</u>
</b> If I had to choose a word to describe it I'd say that this book is ... <b>quiet</b>. Look, quiet is not necessarily a bad thing - it brings a different atmosphere along its path, almost soothing and <b>completely enchanting</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611357._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>① <b>There is a lot of walking in this book</b>, and when I say <i>a lot</i>, picture Frodo and Sam wandering in the Middle-Earth. <i>That</i> kind of walking. <br><br>② <b>The plot is incredibly repetitive</b>, the whole book revolving around the fact that a) Neryn has to go to Shadowfell, b) she doesn't trust (with reasons) Flint, c) she has a power that makes her able to see and talk with fairies and other magical creatures. I won't lie to you, this is highly frustrating at times. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611358._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>③ I might have been under a spell because despite the walking, despite the repetitions, <b>I was never bored</b>, but <i>enchanted</i> and <i>enthralled</i>. Will it be the same thing for you? Fuck if I know. I can't say without doubt that you won't be dying from boredom, but I sure didn't, not for a second, and it was <b>a page-turner</b> for me (trust me, I'm astonished).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611359._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>① <b>Neryn is afraid but fierce, independent, and believable</b> - she wants to be strong but doesn't succeed all the time and that's GREAT. She doesn't trust the first guy coming (I confess that I would have LOVED for her to trust Flint on sight, but hey, I'm weak, she was right, okay, I stop sulking - maybe). And if she sometimes takes risks, it's only because she wants to overcome the obstacles she meets during her quest. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Weapons sharp. Backs straight. Hearts high"</b>
</blockquote><br>If I had some concerns about her personality at the beginning, her courage and her perseverance definitely won me along the way (she's still a little bit of a special snowflake, though).<br><br>② <b>Flint is the best kind of characters</b> : hard to trust, complex, morally ambiguous , <i>conflicted</i>. I can't express how much I'm eager to learn more about him. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Become my friend and you embrace a nightmare. I don't wish that on anyone."</b>
</blockquote><br>I might be crazy, because I felt attracted to this tortured guy from the start. *shrug*<br><br>③ <b>The Little Folk speaks in a dialect</b> that can be unsettling at first : <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Bide ye here awhile. Dinna be afeart o' the shadows; they canna harm ye. Sit quiet; ye look weary tae the bane. I willna be lang."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Strangely, <b>it didn't bother me because a) it's rare and 2) it became easy to translate pretty fast</b>. Don't ask me, I have no idea why, except maybe because it makes sense : contrary to many books that use a dialect, the author goes beyond throwing some words here and there, but uses a coherent language, and once the reader has digested the initial surprise, it becomes more and more easy to follow their conversations. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664090i/15611360._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>① The <b>writing</b> is really, really good, not heavy and flows smoothly. As far as I'm concerned, the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a> writes played a large role in determining my enjoyment. <br><br>② <b>Nothing is ever as straightforward as it seems</b> : indeed while at the beginning the boundaries between good and evil seem to be thick and steady, we quickly realize that nothing is as simple as it appears. Good reasons can lead to bad choices, and the contrary is also true. This world is brutal, unforgiving, and sometimes there's no such thing as a <i>right</i> choice. To be frank, I can't wait to learn more about this world. <br><br>③ Although I can't say when this event occurred, in the end <b>I care about every one of these characters</b> <s>especially Flint. God I love him</s>, and in my opinion that's perhaps the most important of all things, don't you think?<br><br>PS. I don't know why the blurb says that Flint is handsome because <b>he's not</b>, and that's one of the things I loved about him.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_850062371" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/850062371" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/850062371?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer850062371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1970807746543627503"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/08/review-shadowfell-by-juliet-marillier.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>This book . . . was underwhelming.<br/><br/>For the first 100 pages, I was bored out of my eyeballs. It took me three days to read it. B/c bored. THREE DAYS to finish a 400 page YA fantasy. <br/><br/>On the bright side, I was very productive blog-wise . . . b/c I couldn't make myself read . . .<br/><br/>I know I'm beating a dead horse here <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506635210ra/24034897.gif' width='300' height='232' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
 <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (<------not really a spoiler), but I love Juliet Marillier. One of my favorite books of all time is a book by Marillier (<b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13929.Wildwood_Dancing?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wild</a></b></span>
  <span id="freeText1970807746543627503" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/08/review-shadowfell-by-juliet-marillier.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>This book . . . was underwhelming.<br><br>For the first 100 pages, I was bored out of my eyeballs. It took me three days to read it. B/c bored. THREE DAYS to finish a 400 page YA fantasy. <br><br>On the bright side, I was very productive blog-wise . . . b/c I couldn't make myself read . . .<br><br>I know I'm beating a dead horse here <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506635210ra/24034897.gif" width="300" height="232" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (&lt;------not really a spoiler), but I love Juliet Marillier. One of my favorite books of all time is a book by Marillier (<b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13929.Wildwood_Dancing?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildwood Dancing</a>
</b>), and I've very much enjoyed several of her adult fantasy series as well. <br><br>I was expecting this to be a sure thing.<br><br>It wasn't.<br><br>It picked up a bit after those first 100 pages, and I did enjoy the depictions of the Fae as a fractious band of <b>
  <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0091369/?ref_=fn_al_tt_3" rel="nofollow noopener">Labyrinth</a>
</b>-type creatures, but ultimately it all felt very average:<br><br>A tyrannical king has practically snuffed magic out of the world, except for his own private use. A girl with a powerful gift has lost her entire family b/c Tyrannical King. A manboy in a cloak rescues Girl, but is he trustworthy? Girl ditches Manboy to travel to Rebel Base that Girl isn't sure really exists. But Manboy manages to find Girl over and over again.<br><br>Blah, blah, a thousand times BLAH.<br><br>And Neryn (Girl) is a very young heroine, both in age and temperament. The blurb says she's sixteen, but unless she had an unremarked upon birthday somewhere in the book, she's only fifteen, and there is a lot of character growth going on. But it's the timid second-guessing, early adolescent kind of character growth. The, "<i>Can I trust him? I can't trust him. <i>Maybe</i> I can trust him. I'm starting to trust him. HE BETRAYED ME! Did he betray me? He definitely betrayed me. Maybe he didn't betray me. I LOVE him</i>," type of character growth. *bangs head against wall*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408805815ra/10899279.gif" width="245" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408805815ra/10899278.gif" width="500" height="264" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408805815ra/10899280.gif" width="245" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408805815ra/10899281.gif" width="245" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then at the very end (of course), it's Epiphany Time!<br><br>Suddenly Neryn works her way to all the conclusions you've been screaming at her throughout the book. And yeah, better late than never, but b/c of the earlier back and forth, you don't really trust that it will survive the next teenaged bout of gratuitous drama.<br><br>So that was frustrating.<br><br>BUT . . . it wasn't all bad. I adored Flint (Manboy). He was an incredibly complex character, and beyond that, he was a character whom I could admire. He chose to live his life for the greater good, he lives with the consequences of that choice, and they are dire. I <i>might</i> have a <del>fanatical</del> mild case of hero worship . . . Just sayin'.<br><br>And we all know how bloodthirsty I am--I OWN IT--but I don't want to throttle Neryn for being reluctant to KILL THEM ALL.<br><br>"Why not?" you ask<br><br>Well . . . b/c this is the place where Marillier's brilliance finally shines through. Neryn is hesitant to kill others, not b/c she's preoccupied with the state of her soul (me, me, me, me, I, I, I, I *rolls eyes*). Not b/c she's having a pity party knowing that once she begins (*switches to announcer voice*), HER LIFE WILL INEVITABLY BE FILLED WITH DARKNESS AND DEATH (boo-friggin'-hoo). No . . . Neryn is hesitant to kill, b/c through Flint she sees that the king's men are just men. Men fighting on the wrong side, but just men, nevertheless. And she is desperate to find a way to help the rebels that doesn't involve the mass slaughter of men.<br><br>I have no doubt that if it comes down to it, she'll make the hard choice. But Marillier so ingeniously lays the groundwork for Neryn's internal struggle, that even I--violent urges and all--do not cry out for these men's blood.<br><br>*tips hat*<br><br>So not my favorite book, but not a total loss either. And I have it on good authority that book 2 is significantly better, so I'm not ready to give up just yet. Onto RAVEN FLIGHT I go. BUT. *lowers voice ominously* Beware my wrath, if I've been misled . . .<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1970807746543627503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1469699959" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469699959" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1469699959?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469699959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10975795435578872986">I offhandedly bought this series from Book Outlet one day and it's just been sitting on my shelves. I've felt sort of reading slumpy after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Mist and Fury</a>, so I figured a new series would be just what I needed. Never in my wildest dreams did I expect the start of this series to blow me away like it did. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It seemed to me it would be better to die standing up to a tyrant than to survive as a tool of his will.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Shadowfell</i> was everything I could ever want in fae story. It was so </span>
  <span id="freeText10975795435578872986" style="display:none">I offhandedly bought this series from Book Outlet one day and it's just been sitting on my shelves. I've felt sort of reading slumpy after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a>, so I figured a new series would be just what I needed. Never in my wildest dreams did I expect the start of this series to blow me away like it did. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It seemed to me it would be better to die standing up to a tyrant than to survive as a tool of his will.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Shadowfell</i> was everything I could ever want in fae story. It was so magical and whimsical, yet so full of adventure and mystery. Juliet Marillier's writing flows so eloquently that it was impossible not to become addicted to this world after chapter one. <br><br>In this world, some people are blessed with canny gifts. There is a vast array of canny gifts, from being able to see the future, to altering people's minds, to just heightened senses and skills. These are all outlawed and punishable by death, unless it would work in the favor of the king, Keldec. Not only is anything involving these gifts illegal, even talking to or housing fae (or people who have) is punishable by death. <br><br>Autumn is the time of the Cull, and is even more dangerous for wandering travelers. The king's enforcers will kill mercilessly, seeking out these individuals and their entire villages. They do not hesitate...<i>they exhibit no restraint. They take and they take and...</i> Oh my gosh, I am such <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ReTP6x_sDiM" rel="nofollow noopener">Hamilton</a> trash.<br><br>This book surrounds Nerya, who has a very special canny gift. Normally the fae(Good Folk/Little Ones) only can be seen or heard by humans if they wish to do so. Well, Nerya can see and hear them all the time. Obviously it's easy to see how useful that would be for the king, so she has been hunted, and on the run, for a very long time. <br><br>Nerya's life has had a lot of sadness in it, but in her childhood her grandmother taught her some things about the fae. How to offer them food, how iron hurts them and will keep them away, how some things are worth a sacrifice. <br><br>After her father parts with her over three silver, this book becomes an adventure story of Nerya trying to get to Shadowfell. Along the way, the adventure becomes full of quests, questions on who Nerya can trust and, most importantly, survival. <br><br>There is also a little romance, but my bleeding heart wished there was much more. Flint is a double agent in this medieval world, who is also harboring his own secrets. Honestly, I fell in love with him from the start. Juliet Marillier lets the reader know from start to finish that Flint is not the drop dead gorgeous male protagonist we are used to the heroine swooning over, and honestly that made me love him even more. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Be safe, my heart”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Also, I know I said above that the fae in this book are called Good Folk and Little Ones, but they aren't magical humans with pointed ears. No, no, they are little creatures that come in all shapes and sizes. Some even are much more on the animal side when it comes to their looks. I completely loved this version of fae and, like I said before, I easily became addicted to these characters and this world. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, where can I sign up to get cuddled by 20 wolf puppies? Because I need that in my life immediately. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This book was as amazing journey, and I felt so blessed to be able to come along for the ride. The world building is captivating, the prose is beyond gorgeous, and the characters evoked much emotion from me. This was my first Juliet Marillier book, but it will not be my last.<br><br>Like, I'm literally going to binge read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648590421" rel="nofollow noopener">Raven Flight</a> right now. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462659771ra/19027500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10975795435578872986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114843937" />
    <a title="Carla *Jen7waters*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3288963-carla-jen7waters"><img alt="Carla *Jen7waters*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594777797p2/3288963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114843937?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carla *Jen7waters*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carla *Jen7waters*" href="/user/show/3288963-carla-jen7waters">Carla *Jen7waters*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=no-love-triangle">no-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114843937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14434563991423425135"><b>
  <u>Before reading the book</u>
</b> (I can't delete the little fellow, he got me a few likes)<br/><a href='http://www.bookdepository.com/Shadowfell-Juliet-Marillier/9780375869549/?a_aid=jen7waters2' rel='nofollow noopener'>September 11!!</a> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/96501.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>After reading the book</u>
</b><br/><br/>I should probably start this review by saying I’m a HUGE Juliet Marillier fan (for those who don’t know this yet) -- she’s my favorite author, fantasy is my genre of choice, and every time I’m in possession of a new JM book it’s like Christmas, and it’s snowing outside while I’m inside the house by the fire, looking out the window, with a cup of cinnamon flavored hot choc</span>
  <span id="freeText14434563991423425135" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Before reading the book</u>
</b> (I can't delete the little fellow, he got me a few likes)<br><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/Shadowfell-Juliet-Marillier/9780375869549/?a_aid=jen7waters2" rel="nofollow noopener">September 11!!</a> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/96501.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>After reading the book</u>
</b><br><br>I should probably start this review by saying I’m a HUGE Juliet Marillier fan (for those who don’t know this yet) -- she’s my favorite author, fantasy is my genre of choice, and every time I’m in possession of a new JM book it’s like Christmas, and it’s snowing outside while I’m inside the house by the fire, looking out the window, with a cup of cinnamon flavored hot chocolate warming my hands, a blanket over my legs, and I’m about to open the perfect gift, which by the way, would be a JM book.<br><br>That said, <b>Shadowfell</b> tells the story of Neryn’s journey across Alban, a land ruled by the tyrant Keldec -- at first she’s travelling with her father, who after doing something terrible to her, dies and leaves her all alone in the world; after this tragic event she decides to travel to a place in the north called <b>Shadowfell</b>, the alleged land of the rebels, where she believes she’ll be safe from the Enforcers, and from the king himself, because he could use her powers for his benefit. Yes, the girl has powers.<br><br>Naturally I loved this book from page one, and I loved especially how the story picks up rhythm in the first couple of pages and barely slows it down afterwards, there’s always something happening with or around Neryn, something that would make it impossible for me to put the book down.<br><br>AND THE MALE LEAD. Goodness! Juliet really knows how to write them. (Not sure why I sounded surprised just now.) His attitude towards Neryn melted my heart from the very first moment – his posture, his patience, the way the helps and takes care of her even when she’s doubting his motives. Awww. In fact he reminded me a bit of Red, which is always the best compliment I can give to a male character.<br><br>I also loved the secondary characters, mainly the Good Folk who follows Neryn on the journey, their knowledge is crucial for her mission, and they also help her survive along the way -- would give them all a big hug if I could; still my favorites were the Brollachan and the pookie -- the image of a giant using a cat-like creature as a ball he throws in the air is forever stuck in my brain, I’m sure it will be useful for when I’m feeling down. xD<br><br><b>*kind of spoiler ahead, not really if you know Neryn will be heroine of the whole series*</b><br>The end surprised me -- this is the first JM book that ends without the couple actually getting together (don’t even try to contradict me, I know what happened in Seer, they got together, Felix just needed to get some stuff done before), and all I can say is: MY HEART CAN’T TAKE IT! I need them together, I need it! But Neryn will still be the heroine in the second book, so I’m thinking, hoping, <i>praying</i>, they will have plenty of time to get together and leave my heart at peace. I know the wait will be worth it, I just know it.<br><b>*end of spoiler*</b><br><br>What else can I say? I honestly could go on and on about <b>Shadowfell</b> to the point of people reading this review eventually run away screaming, but I’ll stop right now because if I go on more spoilers will find its way out of me and I’d hate for that to happen.<br><br>Buy it, read it, let your minds rejoice in the excellence of Juliet Marillier’s writing--do yourselves the favor.<br><br>Am I right, or am I right, little dancing owls?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380337986ra/695262.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> &lt;- I believe this is a "The human is right, she's right!"<br><br>*PT* <a href="http://cuidadocomodalmata.wordpress.com/2012/10/03/shadowfell/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuidado com o Dálmata</a></span>

<div id="review_493883907" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/493883907" />
    <a title="Amaryllis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6523210-amaryllis"><img alt="Amaryllis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419509622p2/6523210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/493883907?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amaryllis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amaryllis" href="/user/show/6523210-amaryllis">Amaryllis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13574702-shadowfell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=heroine_strong-willed">heroine_strong-willed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=genre_fantasy">genre_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=my-dream-men">my-dream-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=journey-of-self-discovery">journey-of-self-discovery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=hero_nice-guy">hero_nice-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=slow-start">slow-start</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=captivating-storyline">captivating-storyline</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6523210-amaryllis?shelf=genre_young-adult">genre_young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer493883907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11570342484486119346"><u>
  <b>FINDING A CURE FOR MY OBSESSION</b>
</u><br/>AKA MY WRITING THERAPY FOR SHADOWFELL<br/><i>This is not a review, more like the ramblings of an addict.</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784602.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When it comes to Juliet Marillier's stories, I love <b>EVERYTHING</b>. I really do.<br/><br/><i>I love everything from the <b>captivating world-building</b> to the <b>gorgeous, enthralling writing style</b>, and the likeable <b>heroines</b> who, like Neryn, all have a <b>clever, enlightened and strong-willed</b> nature. <br/>I love the tales of these young girls embarking on a <b>learning journey</b> that brings all kinds of </i></span>
  <span id="freeText11570342484486119346" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>FINDING A CURE FOR MY OBSESSION</b>
</u><br>AKA MY WRITING THERAPY FOR SHADOWFELL<br><i>This is not a review, more like the ramblings of an addict.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784602.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When it comes to Juliet Marillier's stories, I love <b>EVERYTHING</b>. I really do.<br><br><i>I love everything from the <b>captivating world-building</b> to the <b>gorgeous, enthralling writing style</b>, and the likeable <b>heroines</b> who, like Neryn, all have a <b>clever, enlightened and strong-willed</b> nature. <br>I love the tales of these young girls embarking on a <b>learning journey</b> that brings all kinds of trials and hardships to them, but always ends with a <b>happily ever after ending</b>, most of their hopes answered and their wishes granted.<br>And, while on the way to freedom, they also find <b>true love</b>. <br>Yes. Everything is perfect.</i><br><br>...<br><br><b>BUT LET'S BE A BIT MORE HONEST.</b><br>Among all of these good things, TRULY, it is the latter that constitutes my obsession : the <b>ROMANCE</b>.<br><br>How to put my infatuation into words ?<br><br><b>
  <u>&gt;&gt; JULIET MARILLIER'S IDEA OF LOVE</u>
</b><br><br>To put it simply, what I like about the romance by Juliet Marillier is her <u>
  <b>depiction of love</b>
</u>.<br><br>I have learned from her books (the ones I've read so far) that <b>LOVE</b> (according to her writing) is a feeling that <b>grows</b> inside you, <b>taking root slowly</b> in your heart. <b>Time and patience help building</b> this feeling into a conviction so <b>strong</b> that, to you, it becomes an all-encompassing religion, the most powerful and deep-rooted belief to <b>guide all of your actions</b>.<br><br>(Moreover in JM's books, the characters fall in love at a <b>realistic</b> pace.)<br><br>On a normal day, I'm the kind of reader who shamelessly drools over sexy Alpha type of men with cocky attitudes, who like to make a habit of falling in desire for their women at the very first glance. (But urgh. Instant attraction gets old.)<br> <br>And, sometimes (those are the best of times), I get the chance to come across a book introducing me to a male character like <b>Flint</b>. <br><b>THAT's when I truly lose it completely.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784603.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>&gt;&gt; ABOUT FLINT, THE MALE LEAD, AND OTHER JULIET MARILLIER'S HEROES</u>
</b><br><br>Like most of JM's heroes, Flint is a <b>confident, skilled and capable</b> man. <br>He's a person of few words, keeping his thoughts to himself mostly, and he scarcely lets any emotion show on his face. <br>However, as indifferent as he seems, we can see immediately that he treats Neryn with unmistakable <b>patience, respect</b>, and what looks suspiciously much like <b>kindness</b>.<br>His secretive behavior doesn't help Neryn lower down her guard though. Because of it, she has a hard time believing in his promises and entrusting herself to his care completely.<br>Yet, no matter what her opinion of him is, Flint <b>keeps looking out for her</b>, not asking for any form of compensation in return.<br>With the growing sense of <b>safety and protection</b> he provides her, Neryn can't help but surrender to the change of feelings taking hold of her.<br><br>(At this point, seeing as I have eagle eyes for details, not to mention a tendency for overanalyzing, I am sure I must have had a know-it-all smile plastered on my goofy face. <br>I was so eager to see the development of Neryn's and Flint's relationship, that I must have looked every bit like the fool who hurries off, as soon as she hears the sound of a storm coming, to stand outside in plain sight and wait for the lightning to come and strike her.)<br><br>But let's get a better look at the reader's reactions, shall we?<br><br><b>
  <u>&gt;&gt; READERS, PREPARE YOURSELVES NOT TO BE YOUR NORMAL SELVES</u>
</b><br><br><i>
  <b>So what happens to the reader in face of such economic display of feelings on the hero's part?</b>
</i><br><br>1) as time passes, far from getting frustrated, you become more and more <b>restless with anticipation and excitement</b><br><br>2) without knowing it, you have built your own personal radar, to <b>warn yourself of <u>ANY</u> progress in the romance department</b><br><br>3) slowly, you find yourself speaking out-loud to Flint, giving him words of <b>encouragement</b> on how to approach the heroine<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784604.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4) at the <b>merest</b> sight of blush forming on Flint's cheeks, <br>at the <b>smallest</b> brush of his fingers, <br>at the <b>tiniest</b> whisper of kind words, <br><i>etc... </i><br><b>in short, at <u>ANY SIGN</u> hinting at the possibility of romantic feelings on his part, YOU BREAK OUT INTO:<br> <br>A GIGGLING FIT,<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784605.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A SCREAMING FIT,<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784606.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A JUMPING FIT,</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784607.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>or in my case, <b>A SALSA FIT</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403304ra/784608.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>I can well explain this kind of pathologic behavior:</u><br>this is the result of having craved a confession of Flint's feelings for so long : therefore, <b>the smallest of his concessions feels like a <i>hard-earned victory</i></b>. <br>Which brings us to the reason for the uncontrollable fits : they simply are the reader's way of dealing with the pent-up anticipation.<br><br><b>
  <u>&gt;&gt; TO SUM IT ALL UP</u>
</b><br><br>Flint has nothing to envy to charming bad boys and their arrogant ways. <br>There's no need for him to show off his best physical attributes, or to demonstrate his badass prowess.<br>No need to seduce by giving words of compliment either.<br><br>But you, reader, would do well to judge him by his actions, for <b>actions speak way louder than words</b>. <br>You will understand quickly that his <b>swoon worthiness</b> lies in his <b>warm steady presence</b>.<br>One of his <b>rare smiles</b> is enough to make you weak in the knees (or in my case, run around in circles like I've just won the lottery). <br><b>SUCH is the level of his masculinity.</b><br><br><b><u>&gt;&gt; CONCLUSION</u><br><br>Juliet Marillier's heroes are the kind of men that you want to marry. <br>Because any woman in her right mind would like to spend her life being forever <i>protected, respected and admired</i>. That's how it feels TO BE LOVED.<b></b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11570342484486119346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_372583744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372583744" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/372583744?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13574702-shadowfell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=arc-galley-and-first-reads">arc-galley-and-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=swoooon">swoooon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer372583744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3254864239698502926">Rating: 3.5 Stars <br/><br/><i> Shadowfell </i> is, I am ashamed to admit, my <i> first </i> Juliet Marillier novel. While I doubt it is her best, I can already see why she has such a huge fan following. Not only is her writing simply beautiful, but her world-building also manages to be exceedingly unique as her story grabs you in, even from the start. Furthermore, each and every one of Marillier’s characters is wonderfully developed, containing an immense amount of depth. While <i> Shadowfell</i>’s main fault seems to lie wi</span>
  <span id="freeText3254864239698502926" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5 Stars <br /><br /><i> Shadowfell </i> is, I am ashamed to admit, my <i> first </i> Juliet Marillier novel. While I doubt it is her best, I can already see why she has such a huge fan following. Not only is her writing simply beautiful, but her world-building also manages to be exceedingly unique as her story grabs you in, even from the start. Furthermore, each and every one of Marillier’s characters is wonderfully developed, containing an immense amount of depth. While <i> Shadowfell</i>’s main fault seems to lie with its protagonist, it is still a thrilling tale that will engage readers and perfectly sets us up for an epic trilogy in the making. <br /><br />It is a dangerous time in Alban, especially for Neryn. King Keldec has nearly wiped out all the magic in the kingdom, but his deadly Enforcers still search for Neryn, a girl rumored to have unique powers. Thus, when Neryn is given off to an enigmatic traveler, Flint, and loses her remaining family, she decides to travel to Shadowfell, a mysterious safe-haven for those with abilities like her who can see the Good Folk. Neryn will soon learn, however, that her journey to Shadowfell may not be as easy as she once thought. You see, Neryn possesses a unique gift – one that has not been seen in Alban for years and has the potential to overthrow Keldec. Yet, to use her gift, Neryn must pass through a series of tasks, all unknown to her, during her travels. Neryn’s journey will not only test her strength and morals, but they will test her bonds of loyalty, friendship, and perhaps even…love. <br /><br /><i> Shadowfell, </i> despite being a novel that I simply loved, mostly because of its genre, was one in which the heroine unfortunately fell flat. When this novel begins, we don’t know much about Neryn and are rather confused by her innate goodness, kindness to the Good Folk, and respect for ancient lore. Yet, as the novel progresses, we slowly begin to understand Neryn a bit more and are able to see the events in her past which have made her the way she is. Still, throughout the novel, Neryn is a very <i> naïve </i> character. In a world filled with desperation, evil, and tragedy, I found it hard to believe that Neryn managed to remain so pure and trusting without having the faults of the world she lived in damage her personality. Furthermore, Neryn constantly fails to learn from her mistakes and there is very little character growth in this installment. Neryn <i> does</i> begin to change during the end of this novel, so I am hopeful that we will be seeing a different Neryn in the sequel, but the Neryn in <i> Shadowfell </i> was quite a disappointment. I admired her resilience, her strength, her kindness, and her hopeful nature, so I definitely did like her and I even understood how so much of her past had made her the way she was, but I was still hoping for something <i> more </i> from her overall which I, unfortunately, did not get to see. <br /><br />Neryn aside, <i> Shadowfell </i> was a remarkable novel. I loved the world-building straight off the bat as it was a unique blend of fey lore and Celtic mythology, combining together to create the Good Folk. Furthermore, the story of Alban was not only extremely interesting, as were the politics of the nation, but it was also something you <i> felt. </i> While originally seeming to be similar to <i> Throne of Glass </i> in the sense that both novels were set in fantasy realms with kings who despite magic, Marillier, unlike Maas, enables us to see and truly witness the misfortune that befalls this nation and Alban itself became a character of its own. Even the Good Folk, who are mysterious creatures, were wonderful to read about and I was thoroughly immersed in the many tales they told, their history, the slow uncovering of their importance to the story, and the many gifts they possessed. <br /><br />Yet, what really made me love <i> Shadowfell </i> was Flint. From the surface, it seems as if Flint is your typical tortured male protagonist. As the story unfolds, however, it is evident that Flint, while remaining to be a tormented character, is also one with an immense amount of courage, strength, and heart. Furthermore, Flint’s pain stems from the fact that he carries a heavy burden – one no one should have to bear – but that only makes him all the more likable, admirable, and ultimately inspirational for it. In other words, there is simply so much more to Flint than what first meets the eye and I fell hard for the budding romance between him and Neryn. It was written with a beautiful subtlety and was incorporated into the story in such a breath-taking manner that I was <i> completely </i> invested in it. I honestly can’t remember being <i> so </i> taken by a romance in a long time, so it was extremely refreshing. Furthermore, Flint really drove this novel forward as the scenes with him in it were much more fast-paced, contained a lot more action, and simply seemed to have more of <i> everything. </i> In other words, it is <i> Flint </i> and not Neryn who controls much of this story and while I found this to be a strange balance of power, I still loved it. <br /><br />Overall, <i> Shadowfell </i> is a great start to a new series. It has all the right ingredients to become a remarkable trilogy and I love the fact that everything is set up so perfectly for us. It is evident that Marillier has a set plan for this series and her lore, ideas, and plans are all very well thought-out and executed. It rarely happens, but I do believe that the sequel to <i> Shadowfell </i> will be a much stronger novel overall. While Neryn did bring the quality of this story down a bit, I still enjoyed it a <i> lot, </i> so if you’re looking out for a new fantasy novel, you should seriously consider picking this one up this month. It may not be Marillier’s best work, but it is a remarkable piece of fiction regardless. <br /><br />You can read this review and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3254864239698502926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3265770898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3265770898" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3265770898?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/52644185-shadowfell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fae-ness">fae-ness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=books-of-my-heart">books-of-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=audio-challenge-2020">audio-challenge-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beautifully-broken-bastards">beautifully-broken-bastards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3265770898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1002107864544546957"><b>This review was originally posted on <a href='http://booksofmyheart.net/2020/04/06/audio-shadowfell-by-juliet-marillier/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'> Books of My Heart</a></b><br/><br/><i>Review copy was received from Publisher. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.</i><br/><br/>Juliet Marillier is a fable teller or what I like to think of as a modern-day Grimm. She weaves these very intricate stories that usually involve humans with hints of the fae and she does this very well. <strong>Shadowfell</strong> is the first book in the, already completed but new to audio, three book <em>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/78224-shadowfell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadowfell</a>
</em> series.  While <strong>Shadowfell</strong> isn</span>
  <span id="freeText1002107864544546957" style="display:none"><b>This review was originally posted on <a href="http://booksofmyheart.net/2020/04/06/audio-shadowfell-by-juliet-marillier/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Books of My Heart</a></b><br /><br /><i>Review copy was received from Publisher. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.</i><br /><br />Juliet Marillier is a fable teller or what I like to think of as a modern-day Grimm. She weaves these very intricate stories that usually involve humans with hints of the fae and she does this very well. <strong>Shadowfell</strong> is the first book in the, already completed but new to audio, three book <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/78224-shadowfell" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadowfell</a>
</em> series.  While <strong>Shadowfell</strong> isn’t my favorite story by Juliet it still has the unique feel Juliet Marillier brings to her stories to transport you into another world.<br /><br />There are some great things this book has going for it. For one it has the orphaned girl who has been on the run for years now and the head of the King’s elite task force who seems to care about her more than he should. That has forbidden love written all over it so I was totally in. Then there are the Fae, I do love a good story with Fae in it. I couldn’t help but root for Neryn as she traveled to find the very secret place of Shadowfell and learns she might have a gift that could save her kind and the Fae too if used on the right side.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It seemed to me it would be better to die standing up to a tyrant than to survive as a tool of his will.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The struggle I had with this as with many fantasy books is all the travelling. Neryn is on the road the majority of the book and while she meets some very cool people along the way most of the time she is alone, or sick, or struggling to get to where she is going and it all felt like it was taking so long. I’ve had this issue before in fantasy and I’ll have it again I’m sure, I usually enjoy the traveling parts in a story as much as other things and so I really wish we would have made it to the resistance earlier in the journey.<br /><br />Still this is a really great introduction into the world and I did love learning what Neryn could possibly be, there is a lot that can be done with that. I even liked the hints that she would eventually have to deal with all the Lords of the Fae so to speak. This is still a very nice faery story, great villain we have yet to see in person but the King is horrible to be sure. I’m definitely continuing on with the series.<br /><br /> 
  <strong>Narration:</strong>
 <br /><br />Henrietta Meire did a fantastic job with the tone of the story and all of the content. She really brought a lot to characters and made the story feel real. With over 100 titles to her narration credit you’d think I’d have heard her before, but this was my first book narrated by her. I was definitely impressed and was able to listen easily at my normal 1.5x speed.<br /><br /><strong>Listen to a clip:  <a href="https://tantor.com/shadowfell-juliet-marillier.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a></strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="1002107864544546957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_367537743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367537743" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367537743?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13574702-shadowfell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=buy-favorites-paper">buy-favorites-paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=review-books-done">review-books-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=emily">emily</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367537743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1592050977653504440">August 2014 re-read: Still just as good. Maybe even better than I'd remembered. I think most will feel the start is slow, but I find this an eminently easy read that's comfortable and enveloping to step into. The prose doesn't seem overt or in-your-face, but it's so perfect at being what it needs to be that you just flow over the words and are swept along.<br/><br/><br/>September 2013 re-read thoughts: I love this even more on a re-read. Solid 4.5 stars. Strong characters, fascinating world, and beautifully de</span>
  <span id="freeText1592050977653504440" style="display:none">August 2014 re-read: Still just as good. Maybe even better than I'd remembered. I think most will feel the start is slow, but I find this an eminently easy read that's comfortable and enveloping to step into. The prose doesn't seem overt or in-your-face, but it's so perfect at being what it needs to be that you just flow over the words and are swept along.<br /><br /><br />September 2013 re-read thoughts: I love this even more on a re-read. Solid 4.5 stars. Strong characters, fascinating world, and beautifully developed storyline. <br /><br />Review: <br /><br />I’d been meaning to pick up a book by Juliet Marillier for years before chance allowed me to get an early copy of <i>Shadowfell</i>. I’m so glad I started here. Ms. Marillier’s prose is evocative and beautiful to read, with lush descriptions that immerse you in the world and make you care about these characters. <i>Shadowfell</i> is a pretty classic quest story, with Neryn setting out to learn her powers, accomplish tasks – which she doesn’t know details about – and finding a place where she can be who she is.<br /><br />Neryn is a character that I instantly related to. She made the decision long ago to live life, something that is much harder than it sounds in the bleak world that Keldec has made of Alba. On the run for much of her life, seeing atrocities that would break others, Neryn let all of that strengthen her resolve. Added to this, she’s unfailingly kind, protective, and smart – if a bit naïve. At just 15 (or 16, the text of my ARC copy did seem to waver on that), it all felt real. She’d experienced some things that made her grow up more quickly than she should have, and she still had an innocence about her that could frustrate me. She did spend a good deal of time sick, and relying on others for help, but I didn’t hold that against her. This was the first time she was really learning about what she was, and assistance was needed. What I loved here was that she still stood strong on her beliefs, needs, and what she needed to do. It endeared me to her. As I’m sure it did Flint – even while it frustrated him to no end.<br /><br />Flint is a very conflicted character. Though I was fairly sure of his true allegiance throughout the book, there was just enough doubt thrown in there for me to question, just enough that I understood when Neyrn didn’t trust him and took some rather risky chances. I would love to see a bit more from Flint’s point of view, but I think the lack of that made me really appreciate what I did get near the end.<br /><br />While the pacing isn’t fast there is a lot happening in <i>Shadowfell</i>. It’s a long journey, and Neryn has to accomplish many things along the way. I was pulled along, desperate to see what happened next, and how Neryn would beat these almost insurmountable odds to make it to her destination. One slight warning, while the book does end at a good stopping point, this is definitely not the end of Neryn’s story. There is a lot more to be told in the next two books. I didn’t think anything of this, because it seems pretty common in fantasy novels, but wanted to be sure others knew that the overall storyline is not tied up in these 400 pages.<br /><br /><i>Shadowfell</i> is the best young-adult fantasy I’ve read in a long time. I enjoyed the story immensely, and connected with the characters. But the world is what will keep me coming back for more. Ms. Marillier has a gift for writing, one that I’m happy to have finally discovered – and I can’t wait for the next book in this trilogy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1592050977653504440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
